	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Edward VII</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Edward VII (disambiguation)">Edward VII (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">King of the United Kingdom and the British Dominions and Emperor of India 1901-1910</div>

<p><b>Edward VII</b> (Albert Edward; 9 November 1841&#160;– 6 May 1910) was <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs" title="List of British monarchs">King</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_India" title="Emperor of India">Emperor of India</a> from 22 January 1901 until his death in 1910.
</p><p>The eldest son of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Albert_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Albert of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">Prince Albert of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a>, Edward was related to royalty throughout Europe. He was <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a> to the British throne and held the title of <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> for longer than any of his predecessors. During the long reign of his mother, he was largely excluded from political power, and came to personify the fashionable, leisured elite. He travelled throughout Britain performing ceremonial public duties, and represented Britain on visits abroad. His tours of North America in 1860 and the Indian subcontinent in 1875 were popular successes, but despite public approval his reputation as a playboy prince soured his relationship with his mother.
</p><p>As king, Edward played a role in the modernisation of the <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="British Home Fleet">British Home Fleet</a> and the reorganisation of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a>. He reinstituted traditional ceremonies as public displays and broadened the range of people with whom royalty socialised. He fostered good relations between Britain and other European countries, especially <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, for which he was popularly called "Peacemaker", but his relationship with his nephew, the <a href="/wiki/German_Emperor" title="German Emperor">German Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm II">Wilhelm II</a>, was poor. The <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_era" title="Edwardian era">Edwardian era</a>, which covered Edward's reign and was named after him, coincided with the start of a new century and heralded significant changes in technology and society, including <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">steam turbine</a> propulsion and the rise of <a href="/wiki/History_of_socialism_in_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="History of socialism in Great Britain">socialism</a>. He died in 1910 in the midst of a constitutional crisis that was resolved the following year by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Act_1911" title="Parliament Act 1911">Parliament Act 1911</a>, which restricted the power of the unelected <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>.
</p>
