data-framerate=&quot;29.97002997003&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:4125s2.ogv" style="width:220px;height:165px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/4125s2.ogv/220px--4125s2.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/4125s2.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:4125s2.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_King_Edward_VII" title="Funeral of King Edward VII">Funeral procession of King Edward VII</a>, London, 1910</div></div></div>
<p>Edward habitually smoked twenty cigarettes and twelve cigars a day. In 1907, a <a href="/wiki/Rodent_ulcer" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodent ulcer">rodent ulcer</a>, a type of cancer affecting the skin next to his nose, was cured with <a href="/wiki/Radium" title="Radium">radium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Towards the end of his life he increasingly suffered from <a href="/wiki/Bronchitis" title="Bronchitis">bronchitis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dnb_12-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dnb-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He suffered a momentary loss of consciousness during a state visit to Berlin in February 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In March 1910, he was staying at <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a> when he collapsed. He remained there to convalesce, while in London Asquith tried to get the Finance Bill passed. The King's continued ill health was unreported and he attracted criticism for staying in France while political tensions were so high.<sup id="cite_ref-dnb_12-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dnb-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On 27 April he returned to Buckingham Palace, still suffering from severe bronchitis. Alexandra returned from visiting her brother, King <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Greece" title="George I of Greece">George I of Greece</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a> a week later on 5 May.
</p><p>On 6 May, the King suffered several heart attacks, but refused to go to bed, saying, "No, I shall not give in; I shall go on; I shall work to the end."<sup id="cite_ref-p151_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p151-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Between moments of faintness, his son the Prince of Wales (shortly to be King <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a>) told him that his horse, Witch of the Air, had won at <a href="/wiki/Kempton_Park_Racecourse" title="Kempton Park Racecourse">Kempton Park</a> that afternoon. The King replied, "Yes, I have heard of it. I am very glad": his <a href="/wiki/Final_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Final words">final words</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dnb_12-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dnb-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> At 11:30&#160;p.m. he lost consciousness for the last time and was put to bed. He died 15 minutes later.<sup id="cite_ref-p151_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p151-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alexandra refused to allow the King's body to be moved for eight days afterwards, though she allowed small groups of visitors to enter his room.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May, the late King was dressed in his uniform and placed in a massive oak coffin, which was moved on 14 May to the throne room, where it was sealed and lay in state, with a guardsman standing at each corner of the bier. Despite the time that had elapsed since his death, Alexandra noted the King's body remained "wonderfully preserved".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> On the morning of 17 May, the coffin was placed on a gun carriage and drawn by black horses to <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster Hall">Westminster Hall</a>, with the new King and his family walking behind. Following a brief service, the royal family left, and the hall was opened to the public; over 400,000 people filed past the coffin over the next two days.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Tuchman" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbara Tuchman">Barbara Tuchman</a> noted in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guns_of_August" title="The Guns of August">The Guns of August</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_King_Edward_VII" title="Funeral of King Edward VII">his funeral</a>, held on 20 May 1910, marked "the greatest assemblage of royalty and rank ever gathered in one place and, of its kind, the last." A royal train conveyed the King's coffin from London to Windsor Castle, where Edward was buried at <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Chapel">St George's Chapel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural depictions of Edward VII of the United Kingdom">Cultural depictions of Edward VII of the United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_eponyms_in_Canada" title="Royal eponyms in Canada">Royal eponyms in Canada</a></div>

empire.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church,_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church%2C_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg/220px-Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church%2C_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church%2C_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg/330px-Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church%2C_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church%2C_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg/440px-Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church%2C_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edward_VII_memorial_in_St_Jude%27s_Church,_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Memorial to Edward VII in <a href="/wiki/St_Jude%27s_Church,_Hampstead_Garden_Suburb" title="St Jude&#39;s Church, Hampstead Garden Suburb">St Jude's Church, Hampstead Garden Suburb</a></div></div></div>
<p>Before his accession to the throne, Edward was the longest-serving heir apparent in British history. He was surpassed by his great-great-grandson <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Charles">Prince Charles</a> on 20 April 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The title Prince of Wales is not automatically held by the heir apparent; it is bestowed by the reigning monarch at a time of his or her choosing.<sup id="cite_ref-clarence_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clarence-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Edward was the longest-serving holder of that title until surpassed by Charles on 9 September 2017; Edward was Prince of Wales between 8 December 1841 and 22 January 1901 (59 years, 45 days). Charles was created Prince of Wales on 26 July 1958 (61&#160;years, 61&#160;days ago).<sup id="cite_ref-clarence_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clarence-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As king, Edward VII proved a greater success than anyone had expected,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> but he was already past the average life expectancy and had little time left to fulfil the role. In his short reign, he ensured that his second son and heir, George V, was better prepared to take the throne. Contemporaries described their relationship as more like affectionate brothers than father and son,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and on Edward's death George wrote in his diary that he had lost his "best friend and the best of fathers&#160;... I never had a [cross] word with him in my life. I am heart-broken and overwhelmed with grief".<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Edward has been recognised as the first truly constitutional British sovereign and the last sovereign to wield effective political power.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Though lauded as "Peacemaker",<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> he had been afraid his nephew, the German Emperor Wilhelm II, would tip Europe into war.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Four years after Edward's death, World War I broke out. The naval reforms he had supported and his part in securing the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> between Britain, France and Russia, as well as his relationships with his extended family, fed the paranoia of the German Emperor, who blamed Edward for the war.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Publication of the official biography of Edward was delayed until 1927 by its author, <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Lee" title="Sidney Lee">Sidney Lee</a>, who feared German propagandists would select material to portray Edward as an anti-German warmonger.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Lee was also hampered by the extensive destruction of Edward's personal papers; Edward had left orders that all his letters should be burned on his death.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent biographers have been able to construct a more rounded picture of Edward by using material and sources that were unavailable to Lee.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian <a href="/wiki/R._C._K._Ensor" class="mw-redirect" title="R. C. K. Ensor">R. C. K. Ensor</a>, writing in 1936, praised the King's political personality:
</p>
<dl><dd>he had in many respects great natural ability. He knew how to be both dignified and charming; he had an excellent memory; and his tact in handling people was quite exceptional. He had a store of varied, though unsystematized, knowledge gathered at first-hand through talking to all sorts of eminent men. His tastes were not particularly elevated, but they were thoroughly English; and he showed much (though not unfailing) comprehension for the common instincts of the people over whom he reigned. This was not the less remarkable because, though a good linguist in French and German, he never learned to speak English without a German accent.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Ensor rejects the widespread notion that the King exerted important influence on British foreign policy, believing he gained that reputation by making frequent trips abroad, with many highly publicized visits to foreign courts. Ensor thought surviving documents showed "how comparatively crude his views on foreign policy were, how little he read, and of what naïve indiscretions he was capable."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Edward received criticism for his apparent pursuit of self-indulgent pleasure, but he received great praise for his affable manners and diplomatic tact. As his grandson Edward VIII wrote, "his lighter side&#160;... obscured the fact that he had both insight and influence."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> "He had a tremendous zest for pleasure but he also had a real sense of duty", wrote J. B. Priestley.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Lord Esher wrote that Edward VII was "kind and debonair and not undignified—but too human".<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Titles.2C_styles.2C_honours_and_arms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles,_styles,_honours_and_arms">Titles, styles, honours and arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Titles, styles, honours and arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_styles">Titles and styles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Titles and styles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>9 November&#160;– 8 December 1841: <i>His Royal Highness</i> The Duke of Cornwall</li>
<li>8 December 1841&#160;– 22 January 1901: <i>His Royal Highness</i> The Prince of Wales</li>
<li>22 January 1901&#160;– 6 May 1910: <i>His Majesty</i> The King</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>British honours<sup id="cite_ref-cp_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Order of the Garter</a>, Knight, <i>9 November 1858</i><sup id="cite_ref-p60_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p60-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Star_of_India" title="Order of the Star of India">Order of the Star of India</a>, Knight Companion, <i>25 June 1861</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-p306_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p306-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Grand Commander, <i>24 May 1866</i><sup id="cite_ref-p308_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p308-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a>, <i>12 February 1863</i></li>

<li><i>1905</i>: Honorary Admiral of the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Navy" title="Swedish Navy">Swedish Navy</a><sup id="cite_ref-p37_161-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p37-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>1908</i>: Honorary General of the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Army" title="Swedish Army">Swedish Army</a><sup id="cite_ref-p37_161-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p37-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary Admiral of the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Navy">Greek Navy</a><sup id="cite_ref-p37_161-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p37-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary General of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Army" title="Norwegian Army">Norwegian Army</a><sup id="cite_ref-p37_161-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p37-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Edward's <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Prince_of_Wales" title="Coat of arms of the Prince of Wales">coat of arms as the Prince of Wales</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">royal arms</a> <a href="/wiki/Difference_(heraldry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Difference (heraldry)">differenced</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Label_(heraldry)" title="Label (heraldry)">label</a> of three points <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">argent</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Inescutcheon" class="mw-redirect" title="Inescutcheon">inescutcheon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Saxony" title="Coat of arms of Saxony">Duchy of Saxony</a>, representing his paternal arms. When he acceded as King, he gained the royal arms undifferenced.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table border="0" align="center" width="70%">

<tbody><tr>
<th width="33%"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward,_Prince_of_Wales_(1841-1901).svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of Arms of Albert Edward, Prince of Wales (1841-1901).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward%2C_Prince_of_Wales_%281841-1901%29.svg/200px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward%2C_Prince_of_Wales_%281841-1901%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="194" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward%2C_Prince_of_Wales_%281841-1901%29.svg/300px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward%2C_Prince_of_Wales_%281841-1901%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward%2C_Prince_of_Wales_%281841-1901%29.svg/400px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Albert_Edward%2C_Prince_of_Wales_%281841-1901%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1550" data-file-height="1500" /></a></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">His godparents were <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_IV_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William IV of Prussia">the King of Prussia</a>, his paternal step-grandmother <a href="/wiki/Duchess_Marie_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Duchess Marie of Württemberg">the Duchess of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a> (for whom <a href="/wiki/Princess_Victoria_of_Saxe-Coburg-Saalfeld" title="Princess Victoria of Saxe-Coburg-Saalfeld">the Duchess of Kent</a>, his maternal grandmother, stood proxy), his great-uncle <a href="/wiki/Prince_Adolphus,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince Adolphus, Duke of Cambridge">the Duke of Cambridge</a>, his step-great-grandmother <a href="/wiki/Princess_Karoline_Amalie_of_Hesse-Kassel" title="Princess Karoline Amalie of Hesse-Kassel">the Dowager Duchess of Saxe-Coburg-Altenburg</a> (for whom <a href="/wiki/Princess_Augusta_of_Hesse-Kassel" title="Princess Augusta of Hesse-Kassel">the Duchess of Cambridge</a>, his great-aunt, stood proxy), his great-aunt <a href="/wiki/Princess_Sophia_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Sophia of the United Kingdom">Princess Sophia</a> (for whom <a href="/wiki/Princess_Augusta_of_Cambridge" title="Princess Augusta of Cambridge">Princess Augusta of Cambridge</a>, his first cousin once-removed, stood proxy) and his great-uncle <a href="/wiki/Prince_Ferdinand_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="Prince Ferdinand of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">Prince Ferdinand of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Letters written by Edward to Lady Randolph may have "signified no more than a flirtation" but were "[w]ritten in a strain of undue familiarity".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">No English or British sovereign has ever reigned under a double name.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
